<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nigerian_female_police.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="667" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Nigerian_female_police.jpg/220px-Nigerian_female_police.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Nigerian_female_police.jpg/330px-Nigerian_female_police.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Nigerian_female_police.jpg/440px-Nigerian_female_police.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nigerian_female_police.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_Police_Force" title="Nigeria Police Force">Nigerian police officer</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Eyo_festival" title="Eyo festival">Eyo festival</a> in Lagos</div></div></div>
<p>Nigeria is home to a <a href="/wiki/Organized_crime_in_Nigeria" title="Organized crime in Nigeria">substantial network of organised crime</a>, active especially in <a href="/wiki/Illegal_drug_trade" title="Illegal drug trade">drug trafficking</a>, shipping heroin from Asian countries to Europe and America; and <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a> from South America to Europe and South Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298"><a href="#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup> Various <a href="/wiki/Confraternities_in_Nigeria" title="Confraternities in Nigeria">Nigerian confraternities</a> or student "campus cults" are active in both organised crime and political violence as well as providing a network of corruption within Nigeria. As confraternities have extensive connections with political and military figures, they offer excellent alumni networking opportunities. The Supreme Vikings Confraternity, for example, boasts that twelve members of the <a href="/wiki/Rivers_State_House_of_Assembly" title="Rivers State House of Assembly">Rivers State House of Assembly</a> are cult members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cults2_299-0"><a href="#cite_note-cults2-299">[299]</a></sup> In lower levels of society, there are the "<a href="/wiki/Area_boys" title="Area boys">area boys</a>", organised gangs mostly active in Lagos who specialise in a mugging and small-scale drug dealing. Gang violence in Lagos resulted in 273 civilians and 84 policemen being killed from August 2000 to May 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is some <a href="/wiki/Piracy_in_the_Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Piracy in the Gulf of Guinea">piracy in the Gulf of Guinea</a>, with attacks directed at all types of vessels. Consistent with the rise of Nigeria as an increasingly dangerous hot spot, 28 of the 30 seafarers kidnapped globally between January and June 2013 were in Nigeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301"><a href="#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup>
</p><p>Internationally, Nigeria is infamous for a form of bank fraud dubbed <i>419</i>, a type of <a href="/wiki/Advance-fee_scam" title="Advance-fee scam">advance-fee scam</a> (named after Section 419 of the Nigerian Penal Code) along with the "Nigerian scam", a form of <a href="/wiki/Confidence_trick" title="Confidence trick">confidence trick</a> practised by individuals and criminal syndicates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302"><a href="#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup> These scams involve a complicit Nigerian bank (the laws being set up loosely to allow it) and a scammer who claims to have money he needs to obtain from that bank. The victim is talked into exchanging bank account information on the premise that the money will be transferred to them and they will get to keep a cut. In reality, money is taken out instead, or large fees (which seem small in comparison with the imaginary wealth to be gained) are deducted. In 2003, the Nigerian <a href="/wiki/Economic_and_Financial_Crimes_Commission" title="Economic and Financial Crimes Commission">Economic and Financial Crimes Commission</a> was created to combat this and other forms of organised financial crime,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303"><a href="#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup> and in some cases, it has succeeded in bringing the <a href="/wiki/Crime_boss" title="Crime boss">crime bosses</a> to justice and even managing to return the stolen money to victims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup>
</p><p>Nigeria has been <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Nigeria" title="Corruption in Nigeria">pervaded by political corruption</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305"><a href="#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup> Nigeria was ranked 136 out of 182 countries in <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a>'s 2014 <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-306"><a href="#cite_note-306">[306]</a></sup> More than $400 billion were stolen from the treasury by Nigeria's leaders between 1960 and 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307"><a href="#cite_note-307">[307]</a></sup> In 2015, incumbent President Muhammadu Buhari said corrupt officials have stolen $150 billion from Nigeria in the last 10 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308"><a href="#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Terrorist_attacks">Terrorist attacks</span></h4>
<p>On March, 28th, 2022, the <a href="/wiki/Abuja%E2%80%93Kaduna_train_attack" title="Abuja–Kaduna train attack">train between Abuja and Kaduna was attacked</a>. 2 bombs exploded and armed men started shooting. 8 persons were killed, more than 60 persons were abducted. The onslaught has been blamed on local bandits. As per June, 17th, 2022, hostages are still being released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309"><a href="#cite_note-309">[309]</a></sup>
</p><p>On Pentecost Sunday, June 5, 2022, armed men detonated explosives and <a href="/wiki/Owo_church_attack" title="Owo church attack">shot at worshippers</a> at St. Francis Catholic Church in <a href="/wiki/Owo" title="Owo">Owo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ondo_State" title="Ondo State">Ondo</a> state. 40 persons were killed. Investigators blame the Islamic State West Africa Province (ISWAP) for the <a href="/wiki/Massacre" title="Massacre">massacre</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Poverty">Poverty</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_Nigeria" title="Poverty in Nigeria">Poverty in Nigeria</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_Nigeria" title="Poverty in Nigeria">Nigeria poverty rates</a> have gone down significantly in the 2010s because of economic growth. The World Bank states Nigeria has had a 7.4% economic growth in July 2019 which has been their highest yet since the <a class="external text" href="https://www.macrotrends.net/countries/NGA/nigeria/gdp-gross-domestic-product#:~:text=Nigeria%20gdp%20for%202018%20was,a%2018.18%25%20decline%20from%202015." rel="nofollow">gross domestic product rate decreased to 2%.</a> While as of May 4, 2020, 40% of Nigerians live in poverty, this number still shows the growth of the developing country, with <a class="external text" href="https://www.macrotrends.net/countries/NGA/nigeria/gdp-gross-domestic-product#:~:text=Nigeria%20gdp%20for%202018%20was,a%2018.18%25%20decline%20from%202015." rel="nofollow">a previously counted 61% of the population living in poverty in 2012.</a> Having made their plans to reduce this number, Nigeria has presented a plan to the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">World Bank Group</a> to lower this number tremendously. Government instability, which affects the rate at which citizens are employed, is the major reason for the poverty levels being higher in certain periods.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Strikes">Strikes</span></h3>
<p>In the last 23 years (as of September 2022), university workers in Nigeria have gone on strike 17 times, or for 57 months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-310"><a href="#cite_note-310">[310]</a></sup> As a result, the 2022 summer semester was cancelled nationwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311"><a href="#cite_note-311">[311]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Nigeria" title="Human rights in Nigeria">Human rights in Nigeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Protesters_at_the_endSARS_protest_in_Lagos,_Nigeria_19.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="681" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Protesters_at_the_endSARS_protest_in_Lagos%2C_Nigeria_19.jpg/220px-Protesters_at_the_endSARS_protest_in_Lagos%2C_Nigeria_19.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Protesters_at_the_endSARS_protest_in_Lagos%2C_Nigeria_19.jpg/330px-Protesters_at_the_endSARS_protest_in_Lagos%2C_Nigeria_19.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Protesters_at_the_endSARS_protest_in_Lagos%2C_Nigeria_19.jpg/440px-Protesters_at_the_endSARS_protest_in_Lagos%2C_Nigeria_19.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Protesters_at_the_endSARS_protest_in_Lagos,_Nigeria_19.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/End_SARS" title="End SARS">End SARS</a> is a decentralised social movement and series of mass protests against <a href="/wiki/Police_brutality" title="Police brutality">police brutality</a> in Nigeria.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Women_in_Tech.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Women_in_Tech.jpg/220px-Women_in_Tech.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Women_in_Tech.jpg/330px-Women_in_Tech.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Women_in_Tech.jpg/440px-Women_in_Tech.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Women_in_Tech.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nigerian" title="Nigerian">Nigerian</a> women in tech</div></div></div>
<p>Nigeria's human rights record remains poor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StateDeptHumanRights2_312-0"><a href="#cite_note-StateDeptHumanRights2-312">[312]</a></sup> According to the U.S. Department of State,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StateDeptHumanRights2_312-1"><a href="#cite_note-StateDeptHumanRights2-312">[312]</a></sup> the most significant human rights problems are the use of excessive force by security forces, impunity for abuses by security forces, arbitrary arrests, prolonged pretrial detention, judicial corruption and executive influence on the judiciary, rape, torture and other cruel, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inhuman_or_degrading_treatment" title="Inhuman or degrading treatment">inhuman or degrading treatment</a> of prisoners, detainees and suspects; harsh and life‑threatening prison and detention centre conditions; human trafficking for prostitution and forced labour, societal violence and vigilante killings, <a href="/wiki/Child_labour_in_Nigeria" title="Child labour in Nigeria">child labour</a>, child abuse and <a href="/wiki/Child_sexual_abuse_in_Nigeria" title="Child sexual abuse in Nigeria">child sexual exploitation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Domestic_violence_in_Nigeria" title="Domestic violence in Nigeria">domestic violence</a>, discrimination based on ethnicity, region and religion.
</p><p>Nigeria is a state party of the <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Elimination_of_All_Forms_of_Discrimination_Against_Women" title="Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Discrimination Against Women">Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Discrimination Against Women</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313"><a href="#cite_note-313">[313]</a></sup> It also has signed the <a href="/wiki/Maputo_Protocol" title="Maputo Protocol">Maputo Protocol</a>, an international treaty on women's rights, and the African Union Women's Rights Framework.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-314"><a href="#cite_note-314">[314]</a></sup> Discrimination based on sex is a significant human rights issue. Forced marriages are common.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315"><a href="#cite_note-315">[315]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Child_marriage_in_Nigeria" title="Child marriage in Nigeria">Child marriage</a> remains common in Northern Nigeria;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316"><a href="#cite_note-316">[316]</a></sup> 39% of girls are married before age 15, although the Marriage Rights Act banning marriage of girls below 18 years old was introduced on a federal level in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-317"><a href="#cite_note-317">[317]</a></sup> There is rampant <a href="/wiki/Polygamy_in_Nigeria" title="Polygamy in Nigeria">polygamy in Northern Nigeria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318"><a href="#cite_note-318">[318]</a></sup> Submission of the wife to her husband and <a href="/wiki/Domestic_violence_in_Nigeria" title="Domestic violence in Nigeria">domestic violence are common</a>. Women have fewer land rights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319"><a href="#cite_note-319">[319]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Maternal_death" title="Maternal death">Maternal mortality</a> was at 814 per 100,000 live births in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-320"><a href="#cite_note-320">[320]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation_in_Nigeria" title="Female genital mutilation in Nigeria">Female genital mutilation is common</a>, although a ban was implemented in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321"><a href="#cite_note-321">[321]</a></sup> In Nigeria, at least half a million suffer from <a href="/wiki/Urogenital_fistula" title="Urogenital fistula">vaginal fistula</a>, largely as a result of lack of medical care.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-322"><a href="#cite_note-322">[322]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-323"><a href="#cite_note-323">[323]</a></sup> Early marriages can result in the fistula.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-324"><a href="#cite_note-324">[324]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Gender_inequality_in_Nigeria" title="Gender inequality in Nigeria">Women face a large amount of inequality</a> politically in Nigeria, being subjugated to a bias that is <a href="/wiki/Sexism" title="Sexism">sexist</a> and reinforced by socio-cultural, economic and oppressive ways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325"><a href="#cite_note-325">[325]</a></sup> Women throughout the country were only politically <a href="/wiki/Emancipation" title="Emancipation">emancipated</a> in 1979.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-326"><a href="#cite_note-326">[326]</a></sup> Yet husbands continue to dictate the votes for many women in Nigeria, which upholds the patriarchal system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ajayi,_Kunle_200723_327-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ajayi,_Kunle_200723-327">[327]</a></sup> Most workers in the <a href="/wiki/Informal_economy" title="Informal economy">informal sector</a> are women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-328"><a href="#cite_note-328">[328]</a></sup> Women's representation in government since independence from Britain is very poor. Women have been reduced to sideline roles in appointive posts throughout all levels of government and still make up a tiny minority of elected officials.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ajayi,_Kunle_200723_327-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ajayi,_Kunle_200723-327">[327]</a></sup> But nowadays with more education available to the public, Nigerian women are taking steps to have more active roles in the public, and with the help of different initiatives, more businesses are being started by women.
</p><p>Under the <a href="/wiki/Sharia_in_Nigeria" title="Sharia in Nigeria">Shari'a</a> penal code that applies to Muslims in twelve northern states, offences such as alcohol consumption, <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Nigeria" title="LGBT rights in Nigeria">homosexuality</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-329"><a href="#cite_note-329">[329]</a></sup> infidelity and theft carry harsh sentences, including amputation, lashing, stoning and long prison terms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKtravel2_330-0"><a href="#cite_note-UKtravel2-330">[330]</a></sup> According to a 2013 survey by the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a>, 98% of Nigerians believe homosexuality should not be accepted by society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pewglobal.org2_331-0"><a href="#cite_note-pewglobal.org2-331">[331]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Nigeria" title="Culture of Nigeria">Culture of Nigeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chinua_Achebe,_1966_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="881" data-file-width="661" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Chinua_Achebe%2C_1966_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Chinua_Achebe%2C_1966_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Chinua_Achebe%2C_1966_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Chinua_Achebe%2C_1966_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Chinua_Achebe%2C_1966_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Chinua_Achebe%2C_1966_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chinua_Achebe,_1966_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Chinua_Achebe" title="Chinua Achebe">Chinua Achebe</a>, winner <a href="/wiki/Booker_Prize" title="Booker Prize">Booker Prize</a> 2007 and <a href="/wiki/Friedenspreis_des_Deutschen_Buchhandels" title="Friedenspreis des Deutschen Buchhandels">Peace Award of the German book trade</a> 2002</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nigerian_literature" title="Nigerian literature">Nigerian literature</a></div><p>Most Nigerian literature is written in <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, partly because this language is understood by most Nigerians. Literature in the <a href="/wiki/Yoruba_language" title="Yoruba language">Yoruba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hausa_language" title="Hausa language">Hausa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Igbo_language" title="Igbo language">Igbo</a> languages (the three most populous peoples in Nigeria) does exist, however, and in the case of the Hausa, for example, can look back on a centuries-old tradition. With <a href="/wiki/Wole_Soyinka" title="Wole Soyinka">Wole Soyinka</a>, Nigeria can present a <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize winner for literature</a>. <a href="/wiki/Chinua_Achebe" title="Chinua Achebe">Chinua Achebe</a> won the prestigious <a href="/wiki/Booker_Prize" title="Booker Prize">Booker Prize</a> in 2007 and <a href="/wiki/Ben_Okri" title="Ben Okri">Ben Okri</a> in 1991. <a href="/wiki/Chinua_Achebe" title="Chinua Achebe">Achebe</a> also won the <a href="/wiki/Friedenspreis_des_Deutschen_Buchhandels" title="Friedenspreis des Deutschen Buchhandels">Peace Award of the German Book Trade</a> in 2002.
</p><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Nigeria" title="Music of Nigeria">Music of Nigeria</a></div>
<p>Many late 20th-century musicians such as <a href="/wiki/Fela_Kuti" title="Fela Kuti">Fela Kuti</a> have famously fused cultural elements of various <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_music" title="Indigenous music">indigenous music</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African-American" title="African-American">African-American</a> <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a> to form Afrobeat which has in turn influenced <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop music</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-332"><a href="#cite_note-332">[332]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B9j%C3%BA_music" title="Jùjú music">JuJu</a> music, which is percussion music fused with traditional music from the Yoruba nation and made famous by <a href="/wiki/King_Sunny_Ad%C3%A9" title="King Sunny Adé">King Sunny Adé</a>, is from Nigeria. <a href="/wiki/Fuji_music" title="Fuji music">Fuji music</a>, a Yoruba percussion style, was created and popularised by Mr Fuji, Alhaji Sikiru <a href="/wiki/Ayinde_Barrister" title="Ayinde Barrister">Ayinde Barrister</a>.
</p><p>Afan Music was invented and popularised by the <a href="/wiki/Ewu" title="Ewu">Ewu</a>-born poet and musician Umuobuarie Igberaese. <a href="/wiki/Kennis_Music" title="Kennis Music">Kennis Music</a> originality started the <a href="/wiki/Afrobeats" title="Afrobeats">Afrobeats movement in Nigeria</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kennis_Music" title="Kennis Music">Kennis Music</a> is widely credited for the evolution of the Nigerian music scene and the rise of many major players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-333"><a href="#cite_note-333">[333]</a></sup> In November 2008, Nigeria's music scene (and that of Africa) received international attention when MTV hosted the continent's first African music awards show in Abuja.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-334"><a href="#cite_note-334">[334]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Nigeria" title="Cinema of Nigeria">Cinema of Nigeria</a></div>
<p>The Nigerian film industry is known as <a href="/wiki/Nollywood" title="Nollywood">Nollywood</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Blend_word" title="Blend word">blend</a> of <i>Nigeria</i> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hollywood_(film_industry)" title="Hollywood (film industry)">Hollywood</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-335"><a href="#cite_note-335">[335]</a></sup>) and is now the second-largest producer of movies in the world, having surpassed Hollywood. Only India's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> is larger. Nigerian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Film_studios" title="Film studios">film studios</a> are based in <a href="/wiki/Lagos" title="Lagos">Lagos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kano_(city)" title="Kano (city)">Kano</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Enugu" title="Enugu">Enugu</a>, and form a major portion of the local economy of these cities. <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Nigeria" title="Cinema of Nigeria">Nigerian Cinema Is Africa's Largest Movie Industry In Terms Of Both Value And The Number Of Movies Produced Per Year</a>. Although Nigerian films have been produced since the 1960s, the country's film industry has been aided by the rise of affordable <a href="/wiki/Digital_cinema" title="Digital cinema">digital filming and editing</a> technologies.
</p><p>The 2009 thriller film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Figurine" title="The Figurine">The Figurine</a></i> heightened the media attention towards the <a href="/wiki/New_Nigerian_Cinema" title="New Nigerian Cinema">New Nigerian Cinema</a> revolution. The film was a critical and commercial success in Nigeria, and it was also screened in international film festivals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thorburn,_Jane2_336-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thorburn,_Jane2-336">[336]</a></sup> The 2010 film <i><a href="/wiki/Ij%C3%A9" title="Ijé">Ijé</a></i> by Chineze Anyaene, overtook <i>The Figurine</i> to become the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films_in_Nigeria" title="List of highest-grossing films in Nigeria">highest-grossing Nigerian film</a>; a record it held for four years until it was overtaken in 2014 by <i><a href="/wiki/Half_of_a_Yellow_Sun_(film)" title="Half of a Yellow Sun (film)">Half of a Yellow Sun</a></i>(2013).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Economist2_337-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Economist2-337">[337]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-338"><a href="#cite_note-338">[338]</a></sup> By 2016, this record was held by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wedding_Party_(2016_film)" title="The Wedding Party (2016 film)">The Wedding Party</a></i>, a film by <a href="/wiki/Kemi_Adetiba" title="Kemi Adetiba">Kemi Adetiba</a>.
</p><p>By the end of 2013, the film industry reportedly hit a record-breaking revenue of ₦1.72 trillion (US$4.1 billion). As of 2014, the industry was worth ₦853.9 billion (US$5.1 billion), making it the third most valuable film industry in the world behind the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. It contributed about 1.4% to Nigeria's economy; this was attributed to the increase in the number of quality films produced and more formal distribution methods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-339"><a href="#cite_note-339">[339]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-340"><a href="#cite_note-340">[340]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T.B._Joshua" title="T.B. Joshua">T.B. Joshua</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_TV" title="Emmanuel TV">Emmanuel TV</a>, originating from Nigeria, is one of the most viewed television stations across Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-341"><a href="#cite_note-341">[341]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festival">Festival</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Festivals_in_Nigeria" title="Festivals in Nigeria">Festivals in Nigeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eyo_Iga_Jump.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2854" data-file-width="2602" decoding="async" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Eyo_Iga_Jump.jpg/220px-Eyo_Iga_Jump.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Eyo_Iga_Jump.jpg/330px-Eyo_Iga_Jump.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Eyo_Iga_Jump.jpg/440px-Eyo_Iga_Jump.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eyo_Iga_Jump.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Eyo_festival" title="Eyo festival">Eyo</a> Iga Olowe Salaye masquerade jumping</div></div></div>
<p>There are many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Festivals_in_Nigeria" title="Festivals in Nigeria">festivals in Nigeria</a>, some of which date to the period before the arrival of the major religions in this ethnically and culturally diverse society. The main Muslim and Christian festivals are often celebrated in ways that are unique to Nigeria or unique to the people of a locality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OnlineNigeria2_342-0"><a href="#cite_note-OnlineNigeria2-342">[342]</a></sup> The Nigerian Tourism Development Corporation has been working with the states to upgrade the traditional festivals, which may become important sources of tourism revenue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oxford20102_343-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oxford20102-343">[343]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Nigerian_cuisine" title="Nigerian cuisine">Nigerian cuisine</a>, like West African cuisine in general, is known for its richness and variety. Many different spices, herbs, and flavourings are used in conjunction with <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">palm oil</a> or <a href="/wiki/Peanut" title="Peanut">groundnut</a> oil to create deeply flavoured sauces and soups often made very hot with <a href="/wiki/Chili_pepper" title="Chili pepper">chilli peppers</a>. Nigerian feasts are colourful and lavish, while aromatic market and roadside snacks cooked on barbecues or fried in oil are plentiful and varied. <a href="/wiki/Suya" title="Suya">Suya</a> is usually sold in urban areas especially during night-time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-344"><a href="#cite_note-344">[344]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fashion">Fashion</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fashion_in_Nigeria" title="Fashion in Nigeria">Fashion in Nigeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ituen_Basi_Nigerian_designer_Fashion_Insider_Nov_2018.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="527" data-file-width="866" decoding="async" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Ituen_Basi_Nigerian_designer_Fashion_Insider_Nov_2018.jpg/220px-Ituen_Basi_Nigerian_designer_Fashion_Insider_Nov_2018.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Ituen_Basi_Nigerian_designer_Fashion_Insider_Nov_2018.jpg/330px-Ituen_Basi_Nigerian_designer_Fashion_Insider_Nov_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Ituen_Basi_Nigerian_designer_Fashion_Insider_Nov_2018.jpg/440px-Ituen_Basi_Nigerian_designer_Fashion_Insider_Nov_2018.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ituen_Basi_Nigerian_designer_Fashion_Insider_Nov_2018.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ituen Basi, Lagos based Nigerian fashion designer</div></div></div>
<p>The fashion industry in Nigeria contributes significantly to the country's economics. Casual attire is commonly worn but formal and traditional styles are also worn depending on the occasion. Nigeria is known not only for its fashionable textiles and garments, but also for its fashion designers who have increasingly gained international recognition. <a href="/wiki/Euromonitor_International" title="Euromonitor International">Euromonitor</a> estimates the <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan</a> fashion <a href="/wiki/Market_(economics)" title="Market (economics)">market</a> to be worth $31 billion, with Nigeria accounting for 15% of these $31 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-345"><a href="#cite_note-345">[345]</a></sup> Nigeria is not only known for their many fashion textiles and garment pieces that are secret to their culture. They also outputted many fashion designers who have develop many techniques and business along the way.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sports_in_Nigeria" title="Sports in Nigeria">Sports in Nigeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NIG-ARG_(2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="945" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/NIG-ARG_%282%29.jpg/220px-NIG-ARG_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/NIG-ARG_%282%29.jpg/330px-NIG-ARG_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/NIG-ARG_%282%29.jpg/440px-NIG-ARG_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NIG-ARG_(2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nigeria_national_football_team" title="Nigeria national football team">Nigeria</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a></div></div></div>
<p>Football is largely considered Nigeria's national sport, and the country has its own <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_Professional_Football_League" title="Nigeria Professional Football League">Premier League</a> of football. <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_national_football_team" title="Nigeria national football team">Nigeria's national football team</a>, known as the "Super Eagles", has made the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a> on six occasions <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">1994</a>, <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1998 FIFA World Cup">1998</a>, <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">2002</a>, <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010</a>, <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018</a>. In April 1994, the Super Eagles ranked 5th in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Rankings" title="FIFA World Rankings">FIFA World Rankings</a>, the highest-ranking achieved by an African football team. They won the <a href="/wiki/Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="Africa Cup of Nations">African Cup of Nations</a> in <a href="/wiki/1980_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="1980 African Cup of Nations">1980</a>, <a href="/wiki/1994_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="1994 African Cup of Nations">1994</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2013_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2013 Africa Cup of Nations">2013</a>, and have also hosted the U-17 &amp; U-20 World Cup. They won the gold medal for football in the <a href="/wiki/1996_Summer_Olympics" title="1996 Summer Olympics">1996 Summer Olympics</a> (in which they beat Argentina) becoming the first African football team to win gold in Olympic football.
</p><p>The nation's <a href="/wiki/1993_FIFA_U-17_World_Championship" title="1993 FIFA U-17 World Championship">1993</a> <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_national_under-17_football_team" title="Nigeria national under-17 football team">cadet team</a> produced some international players.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NIG-ARG_(9).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="935" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/NIG-ARG_%289%29.jpg/220px-NIG-ARG_%289%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/NIG-ARG_%289%29.jpg/330px-NIG-ARG_%289%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/NIG-ARG_%289%29.jpg/440px-NIG-ARG_%289%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NIG-ARG_(9).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nigerian football supporters at the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a> in Russia</div></div></div>
<p>Nigeria is also involved in other sports such as basketball, cricket and track and field.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-346"><a href="#cite_note-346">[346]</a></sup> Boxing is also an important sport in Nigeria;.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-347"><a href="#cite_note-347">[347]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_men%27s_national_basketball_team" title="Nigeria men's national basketball team">Nigeria's national basketball team</a> made the headlines internationally when it became the first African team to beat the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_basketball_team" title="United States men's national basketball team">United States men's national team</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-348"><a href="#cite_note-348">[348]</a></sup> In earlier years, Nigeria qualified for the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="Basketball at the 2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a> as it beat heavily favoured world elite teams such as <a href="/wiki/Greece_men%27s_national_basketball_team" title="Greece men's national basketball team">Greece</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lithuania_men%27s_national_basketball_team" title="Lithuania men's national basketball team">Lithuania</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-349"><a href="#cite_note-349">[349]</a></sup> Nigeria has been home to numerous internationally recognised basketball players in the world's top leagues in America, Europe and Asia. These players include <a href="/wiki/Naismith_Memorial_Basketball_Hall_of_Fame" title="Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame">Basketball Hall of Famer</a> <a href="/wiki/Hakeem_Olajuwon" title="Hakeem Olajuwon">Hakeem Olajuwon</a>, and later players in the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">NBA</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Nigerian_Premier_League_(basketball)" title="Nigerian Premier League (basketball)">Nigerian Premier League</a> has become one of the biggest and most-watched basketball competitions in Africa. The games have aired on <i>Kwese TV</i> and have averaged a viewership of over a million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-350"><a href="#cite_note-350">[350]</a></sup>
</p><p>Nigeria made history by qualifying the first <a href="/wiki/Bobsleigh" title="Bobsleigh">bobsled</a> team for the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games" title="Winter Olympic Games">Winter Olympics</a> from Africa when their women's two-person team qualified for <a href="/wiki/Bobsleigh_at_the_2018_Winter_Olympics" title="Bobsleigh at the 2018 Winter Olympics">the bobsled competition</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2018_Winter_Olympics" title="2018 Winter Olympics">XXIII Olympic Winter Games</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-351"><a href="#cite_note-351">[351]</a></sup> In the early 1990s, <a href="/wiki/Scrabble" title="Scrabble">Scrabble</a> was made an official sport in Nigeria. By the end of 2017, there were around 4,000 players in more than 100 clubs in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-352"><a href="#cite_note-352">[352]</a></sup>  In 2018, the Nigerian Curling Federation was established to introduce a new sport to the country with the hope of getting the game to be a part of the curriculum at the elementary, high school, and university levels respectively. At the <a href="/wiki/2019_World_Mixed_Doubles_Curling_Championship" title="2019 World Mixed Doubles Curling Championship">2019 World Mixed Doubles Curling Championship</a> in Norway, Nigeria won their first international match beating France 8–5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-353"><a href="#cite_note-353">[353]</a></sup>
</p><p>Nigeria featured women's and men's national teams in <a href="/wiki/Beach_volleyball" title="Beach volleyball">beach volleyball</a> that competed at the <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%932020_CAVB_Beach_Volleyball_Continental_Cup" title="2018–2020 CAVB Beach Volleyball Continental Cup">2018–2020 CAVB Beach Volleyball Continental Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-354"><a href="#cite_note-354">[354]</a></sup> The country's U21 national teams qualified for the 2019 <a href="/wiki/FIVB_Beach_Volleyball_U21_World_Championships" title="FIVB Beach Volleyball U21 World Championships">FIVB Beach Volleyball U21 World Championships</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-355"><a href="#cite_note-355">[355]</a></sup>
</p>
